<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">List of tallest buildings</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"><div class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint nomobile" id="mw-fr-revisiontag"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><img alt="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page." class="flaggedrevs-icon" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/doc-magnify.png" title="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page."/><img alt="show/hide details" class="fr-toggle-arrow" id="mw-fr-revisiontoggle" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/arrow-down.png" style="display:none;"/></div>

The 828-metre (2,717 ft) tall <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> has been the world's tallest building since 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The Burj Khalifa has been classified as <i>Megatall</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CTBUH_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-CTBUH-2">[2]</a></sup></div>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:487px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tallest_buildings_in_the_world.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1969" data-file-width="4961" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Tallest_buildings_in_the_world.png/485px-Tallest_buildings_in_the_world.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Tallest_buildings_in_the_world.png/728px-Tallest_buildings_in_the_world.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Tallest_buildings_in_the_world.png/970px-Tallest_buildings_in_the_world.png 2x" width="485"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tallest_buildings_in_the_world.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tallest buildings in the world.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This <b>list of tallest buildings in the world</b> ranks <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">skyscrapers</a> by height. Only buildings with continuously occupiable floors are included, thus <a href="/wiki/Nonbuilding_structure" title="Nonbuilding structure">non-building structures</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Tower" title="Tower">towers</a>, are not included. (See <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_and_structures" title="List of tallest buildings and structures">List of tallest buildings and structures</a>.)</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranking_criteria_and_alternatives">Ranking criteria and alternatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_tallest_buildings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Ranking criteria and alternatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The international non-profit organization <a href="/wiki/Council_on_Tall_Buildings_and_Urban_Habitat" title="Council on Tall Buildings and Urban Habitat">Council on Tall Buildings and Urban Habitat</a> (CTBUH) was formed in 1969 and announces the title of "The World's Tallest Building" and sets the standards by which buildings are measured. It maintains a list of the 100 tallest completed buildings in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CTBUH_top_100_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-CTBUH_top_100-3">[3]</a></sup> The organization currently ranks <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a> in Dubai as the tallest at 828 m (2,717 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CTBUH_top_100_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-CTBUH_top_100-3">[3]</a></sup> The CTBUH only recognizes buildings that are complete, however, and some buildings listed within these list articles are not considered complete by the CTBUH.</p>
<p>In 1996, as a response to the dispute as to whether the <a href="/wiki/Petronas_Towers" title="Petronas Towers">Petronas Towers</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Willis_Tower" title="Willis Tower">Sears Tower</a> was taller,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PetronasSears_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-PetronasSears-4">[4]</a></sup> the council listed and ranked buildings in four categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>height to structural or architectural top;</li>
<li>height to floor of highest occupied floor;</li>
<li>height to top of roof (removed as category in November 2009);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> and</li>
<li>height to top of any part of the building.</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Spire" title="Spire">Spires</a> are considered integral parts of the architectural design of buildings, to which changes would substantially change the appearance and design of the building, whereas antennas may be added or removed without such consequences. The Petronas Towers, with their spires, are thus ranked higher than the Willis Tower (formerly the Sears Tower) with its antennas, despite the Petronas Towers' lower roofs and lower highest point.</p>
<p>Until 1996, the world's tallest building was defined by the height to the top of the tallest architectural element, including spires but not antennae. This led to a rivalry between the Bank of Manhattan Building and the <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_Building" title="Chrysler Building">Chrysler Building</a>. The Bank of Manhattan Building employed only a short spire and was 927 ft (283 m) tall and had a much higher top occupied floor (the second category in the 1996 criteria for tallest building). In contrast, the Chrysler Building employed a very large 125 ft (38 m) spire secretly assembled inside the building to claim the title of world's tallest building with a total height of 1,048 ft (319 m), although it had a lower top occupied floor and a shorter height when both buildings' spires were excluded.</p>
<p>Upset by Chrysler's victory, Shreve &amp; Lamb, the consulting architects of the Bank of Manhattan Building, wrote a newspaper article claiming that their building was actually the tallest, since it contained the world's highest usable floor. They pointed out that the observation deck in the Bank of Manhattan Building was nearly 100 ft (30 m) above the top floor in the Chrysler Building, whose surpassing spire was strictly ornamental and inaccessible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>At present, the Burj Khalifa tops the list by some margin, regardless of which criterion is applied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tallest_buildings_in_the_world_.28300_m.2B.29">Tallest buildings in the world (300 m+)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_tallest_buildings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Tallest buildings in the world (300 m+)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of 2016, this list includes all <b>135</b> buildings (completed and architecturally <a href="/wiki/Topping_out" title="Topping out">topped out</a>) which reach a height of 300 metres (984 ft) or more as assessed by their highest architectural feature. Seven of the last eight buildings to have held the record as '<a href="/wiki/Skyscraper#History_of_the_tallest_skyscrapers" title="Skyscraper">tallest building</a>' are still found in the list, with the exception being the North Tower of the original <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973%E2%80%932001)" title="World Trade Center (1973–2001)">World Trade Center</a> after its <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">destruction in the September 11 attacks</a> of 2001.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_with_the_most_entries_in_the_list">Countries with the most entries in the list</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_tallest_buildings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Countries with the most entries in the list">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The countries with three or more entries in the above list of <b>135</b> buildings are:</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:right">
<tr>
<th>Country</th>
<th>Number<br/>
of buildings</th>
<th>Percent<br/>
of total</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a></td>
<td>60</td>
<td>45%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a></td>
<td>26</td>
<td>19%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></td>
<td>19</td>
<td>14%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a></td>
<td>5</td>
<td>4%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a></td>
<td>5</td>
<td>4%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a></td>
<td>3</td>
<td>2%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a></td>
<td>3</td>
<td>2%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left">Others</td>
<td>14</td>
<td>10%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left"><b>Total</b></td>
<td><b>135</b></td>
<td><b>100%</b></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The count for China includes six in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and, with the exception of a dozen buildings, all are relatively new, having been completed in and after 2010. Worldwide, as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_world#Buildings_under_construction" title="List of tallest buildings in the world">there are plans</a> in the next five years for more than 80 buildings in the same height range (including about 40 in China), then the list should have a total of about 200 buildings by the year 2020.</p>

The top 15 floors are occupied by the Ritz-Carlton Hotel Company, the world's highest 6-star grand hotel.</p>

<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px">

<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Wilshire_Grand_Center" title="Wilshire Grand Center">Wilshire Grand Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, became the tallest building in the United States west of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> following its topping out in March 2016.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_measurements">Alternative measurements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_tallest_buildings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Alternative measurements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Height_to_pinnacle_.28highest_point.29">Height to pinnacle (highest point)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_tallest_buildings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Height to pinnacle (highest point)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tallest_Buildings_in_the_World_by_pinnacle_height.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1969" data-file-width="4961" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tallest_Buildings_in_the_World_by_pinnacle_height.png/400px-Tallest_Buildings_in_the_World_by_pinnacle_height.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tallest_Buildings_in_the_World_by_pinnacle_height.png/600px-Tallest_Buildings_in_the_World_by_pinnacle_height.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tallest_Buildings_in_the_World_by_pinnacle_height.png/800px-Tallest_Buildings_in_the_World_by_pinnacle_height.png 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tallest_Buildings_in_the_World_by_pinnacle_height.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tallest buildings by pinnacle height, including all masts, poles, antennae, etc. in 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This measurement disregards distinctions between architectural and non-architectural extensions, and simply measures to the highest point. This measurement is useful for <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_obstacle" title="Air traffic obstacle">air traffic obstacle</a> determinations, and is also a wholly objective measure. However, this measurement includes extensions that are easily added, removed, and modified from a building and are independent of the overall structure.</p>
<p>This measurement only recently came into use, when the <a href="/wiki/Petronas_Towers" title="Petronas Towers">Petronas Towers</a> passed the Sears Tower (now called <a href="/wiki/Willis_Tower" title="Willis Tower">Willis Tower</a>) in height. The former was considered taller because its spires were considered architectural, while the latter's antennae were not. This led to the split of definitions, with the Sears Tower claiming the lead in this and the height-to-roof (now highest occupied floor) categories, and with the Petronas claiming the lead in the architectural height category.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Buildings_under_construction">Buildings under construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_tallest_buildings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Buildings under construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This is a list of <b>80</b> buildings taller than 300 metres or 65 floors that are currently under construction. More than half of the buildings are located in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_tallest_buildings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dd><b>A.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note01.5E"><a href="#ref_note01.5E"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Destroyed buildings not included</dd>
<dd><b>B.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note02.5E"><a href="#ref_note02.5E"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Topped out but not completed.</dd>
<dd><b>C.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note03.5E"><a href="#ref_note03.5E"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Topped out in 1992, when construction was halted. Work was restarted in 2008, exterior work completed in 2011; interior work still ongoing.</dd>
</dl>
